         <h2 class="post-title" style="display:none;">
          <a href="http://blog.lululemon.com/bulletproof-coffee/">
           bulletproof coffee
          </a>
         </h2>
         <a class="social-share-facebook">
         </a>
         <a class="social-share-twitter">
         </a>
         <a class="social-share-googleplus">
         </a>
         <a class="social-share-pinterest">
         </a>
         <a class="social-share-email">
         </a>
        </div>

       <div class="span9 content group" id="content-single">
        <div class="post-57146 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-au category-eu category-food-and-drink category-hk category-na category-nz category-uk hentry-post group blog-big" id="post-57146">
         <!-- post featured &amp; title -->
         <div class="blog-post-header">
          <h1 class="OneLinkNoTx">
           bulletproof coffee
          </h1>
          <p>
           posted: August 16, 2014
          </p>
          <hr/>
         </div>
         <!-- post content -->
         <div class="the-content single group">
          <div class="OneLinkNoTx">
           <p>
            <img alt="Bulletproof Coffee lululemon blog header" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-57287" height="400" src="/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/Bulletproof-Coffee-lululemon-blog-header.jpeg" width="600"/>
            <br/>
            <em>
             How many spoonfuls of butter would you like with your coffee?
            </em>
            <br/>
            <br/>
            When was the last time you reached for oil and butter when making your morning coffee? Its not exactly the first thing that comes to handor mind. But, thats what the man behind
            <a href="http://www.bulletproofexec.com/" target="_blank">
             Bulletproof Coffee
            </a>
            wants to convince us to do.
           </p>
           <p>
            Dave Asprey is the new powerplayer on the coffee scene, a surprising turn for those who know him since he once went five years without a drop. He hated how coffee turned his emotions into a rollercoaster ride with ups, downs, warp speeds and loops.
           </p>
           <p>
            All that changed on a trip to Tibet, when Asprey stumbled into a guest house while trekking at 18,000 feet. There, his hosts offered him a traditional yak butter tea. He spent the next couple of years trying to figure out why the creamy concoction made him feel completely rejuvenated, and finally Bulletproof Coffee was born. (Note: many claim that Paleo diet guru
            <a href="http://robbwolf.com" target="_blank">
             Robb Wolf
            </a>
            has been promoting a similar version of the brew for almost a decade.)
           </p>
           <p>
            You wouldnt be the first one to try it. For more than a decade, one holistic health expert has been doling out doses of butter coffee to his clients,
            <a href="http://www.musclemag.com/should-you-drink-bulletproof-coffee/" target="_blank">
             Muscle Mag
            </a>
            reports. And curiosity about the supposedly super-powered coffee has been growing so quickly that even coffee shops have started selling the in-demand product.
           </p>
           <p>
            <img alt="Nick Odorisio" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-57159" height="399" src="/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/Nick-Odorisio.jpg" width="600"/>
            <br/>
            <em>
             lululemon ambassador, boxer, and gym owner Nick Odorisio swears by making his coffee bulletproof
            </em>
            <br/>
            <br/>
            Our Philadelphia based ambassador, boxer and personal trainer
            <a href="http://www.nicksgym.net/" target="_blank">
             Nick Odorisio
            </a>
            says he drinks it for the energy factor. Its a great start to my morning. It provides satiety and I dont feel hungry for hours. He adds that for some reason butter doesnt bother him in this drink form, though he cant drink milk or soymilk.
           </p>
           <p>
            All someone needs to feel like a superhero all day is three ingredients and some time for a
            <a href="https://www.bulletproofexec.com/how-to-make-your-coffee-bulletproof-and-your-morning-too/" target="_blank">
             coffee-brewing process
            </a>
            Asprey calls meditative. (Others may call it long.)
           </p>
           <p>
            Asprey recommends using a French press or pour-over method with a metal filter for about four minutes to brew his trademarked Bulletproof Coffee Beans (a 12-ounce bag will cost you $18.95 US). While the coffee is brewing, preheat a blender, so your coffee stays warm. Plop in two tablespoons of bright yellow organic butter from grass-fed cows and one tablespoon of MCT oil. Blend, blend, blend, then enjoy a creamy, delicious cup of Bulletproof Coffee followed by a day of mental acuity, increased energy and no food cravings. (Scroll to bottom for two more recipes.)
           </p>
           <p>
            Still, the idea of having three tablespoons of oil and butter a day can be a little much for some people, and there are experts crying foul over how many calories and how much fat is in one cup. When our Houston-based ambassador and yoga instructor
            <a href="http://instagram.com/josie_grossie35" target="_blank">
             Josie Unseth
            </a>
            s peers recommended she try bulletproof coffee to satiate hunger pangs, she wasnt as quick to jump on board.
           </p>
           <p>
            <img alt="Josie Unseth" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-57161" height="800" src="/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/Josie-Unseth.jpg" width="600"/>
            <br/>
            <em>
             lululemon ambassador Josie Unseth has had bulletproof coffee every single day since she first tried it
            </em>
            <br/>
           </p>
           <p>
            I thought it sounded completely nasty, but I committed to try it once because [my colleague] had a theory that I wasnt eating enough fatthe healthy kindsto feel satisfied. I waited a few days to try it because the idea really freaked me out, she says.
           </p>
           <p>
            Still, it only took one cup to get her hooked. Its delish! Sweet, salty, creamy, coffee-tastic goodness. And guess, what? It makes me feel full. Hallelujah!
           </p>
           <p>
            Nick says the fat content makes him feel both decadent and contrarian. Decadent because the creamy taste of the coffee makes it feel like a forbidden Starbucks calorie bomb drink. Contrarian because its in direct contrast to mainstream ideas of nutrition that fat is bad. Some people are deathly afraid of a little fat but fat is flavour, and when you take fat out you have to replace it with something that is typically a chemical, coffee, he says.
           </p>
           <p>
            Its hard to deny wanting the benefits Asprey claims to hold the key toincreased brain power, controlled appetite and boundless energybut only time will tell how bulletproof the new coffees subscribers are.
            <br/>
           </p>
           <div style="border-bottom: 4px; border-style: double;">
           </div>
           <h3>
            Nicks Bulletproof Coffee Recipe
           </h3>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Ingredients
            </strong>
            :
            <br/>
            1 cup earthy, dark coffee (I like local brand
            <a href="http://www.lacolombe.com/mobile/" target="_blank">
             Lacolombe
            </a>
            )
            <br/>
            2 tbsp Kerrygold grass-fed organic butter
            <br/>
            1-2 tbsp pressed virgin coconut oil
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Method
            </strong>
            :
            <br/>
            Make your coffee with a pour-over method or French press. Then place all ingredients into a Vitamix and crank it up to 10, until it froths.
           </p>
           <h3>
            Josies Bulletproof Coffee Recipe
           </h3>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Ingredients
            </strong>
            :
            <br/>
            2 shots espresso
            <br/>
            1 cup hot water
            <br/>
            1 tbsp Kerrygold grass-fed organic butter
            <br/>
            1 tsp organic coconut oil
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Method
            </strong>
            :
            <br/>
            Put all ingredients into a Magic Bullet for about five seconds, whipping until frothy.
            <br/>
            <img alt="Bulletproof coffee ingredients" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-57157" height="903" src="/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/Bulletproof-coffee-ingredients.jpg" width="600"/>
           </p>
           <div style="border-bottom: 4px; border-style: double;">
           </div>
           <p>
            <em>
             <a href="http://aleksagan.com" target="_blank">
              Aleksandra Sagan
             </a>
             is a freelance writer who loves covering millennial and post-secondary issues. Shes an avid runner and health buff, who frequently blogs about her fitness and finance goals on her website. She loves to cook healthy food with lots of spices in her kitchen, but has an irrational fear of baking and the precise measurements it requires.
            </em>
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>

Still sceptical? Do your research and find out why people should stop ingesting it &amp; start lobbying against food companies pouring it into most products. Read the labels.                      <br/>
                     2 tbsp. butter (unsalted)
                     <br/>
                     1 tbsp. coconut oil
                     <br/>
                     1 tbsp. whipcream
                     <br/>
                     if I want a more chai flavor I add 1/4 or so of cinnamon, if I want it sweeter I add a tad of Stevenia.  the whip cream gives it an even creamier flavor and adds to the fat content which is why we drink it right, for the good fats.

                   Im on an adrenal protocol now so I skip the coffee and make Crio Bru, which is roasted and ground cocoa beans made in a french press. I add a bit of cacao powder, and its like a creamy, coconutty, mocha! Best way to start my morning.
                  </p>

                  <p>
                   I am so disappointed in a health-focused company providing this kind recommendation. This concoction is meant to go hand-in-hand with a low-carb ketosis-focused diet, as the diet itself provides no energy. The coffee with oil and butter is meant to send direct energy to your brain, as your brain is not being fed glucose, aka carbs, aka the stuff that our bodies rely on for energy and efficiency. After losing a ton of weight on a plant-based high carb diet, I find it astonishing that people are still giving into these fads. Surely eating/drinking fat cannot permanently make you lose fat. I would do some research on the dangers of these kinds of diet trends before posting.

               <li class="comment odd alt depth-3" id="li-comment-2485596">
                <div class="offset2 span7">
                 <div class="comment-container" id="comment-2485596">
                  <div class="row">
                   <div class="comment-author vcard span3">
                    <div class="row">
                     <div class="span1">
                      <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-64 photo" height="64" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/f5376bddabd3bb243ff03eda051e5c15?s=64&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2F1.gravatar.com%2Favatar%2Fad516503a11cd5ca435acc9bb6523536%3Fs%3D64&amp;r=PG" width="64"/>
                     </div>

                   </div>
                   <!-- .comment-author .vcard -->
                   <div class="comment-content span4">
                    <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata comment-author-name comment-date span2">
                     <!-- author name -->
                     <cite class="fn OneLinkNoTx">
                      ASjerp
                     </cite>
                     <!-- date -->
                     <a href="http://blog.lululemon.com/bulletproof-coffee/#comment-2485596">
                      Jan 25, 2015
                     </a>
                     <!-- reply -->
                    </div>
                    <!-- .reply -->
                    <div>
                     <div class="comment-body OneLinkNoTx">
                      <p>
                       Actually Tessa, I would say Mary has put more research into her comment than most others  Our bodies do require carbohydrate to feed the brain glucose, hence why our preferred energy storage is glycogen (with excess energy being converted to fat).  Recruitment of endogenous glucose synthesis is associated with starvation syndromes and lessening of basal metabolic rate.  Ketosis occurs when the body has depleted all glucose and then all glycogen reserves in the liver and then muscles.  When fatty acids are broken down to produce glucose for brain function (and if you dont have enough, your lean tissue reserves will also start to be broken down) there is a release of ketone bodies.  The danger of ketosis is that is causes the body to enter a state of acidosis  a plasma pH variation outside of 7.35-7.45 is ultimately fatal.  Long term, your bodies buffering systems can be compromised such that increasing acid begins to damage the kidneys, before acidosis results.  All nutritional biochemistry aside, the key to good health and successful long term weight loss is no big secret.  Increase lean protein intake, choose low-fat options (providing low fat doesnt equate to high sugar), eat complex carbohydrates from whole grains, eat more and a variety of non-starch fruits &amp; vegetables, keep overall fat intake to less than 25% of total caloric intake (biased towards polyunsaturated fats containing linoleic and linolenic essential fatty acids ), total saturated fat intake should be around 5% (some people can tolerate higher without negative effects).
                      </p>
                      <p>
                       As for bulletproof coffee  so long as you are keeping your total dietary saturated fat intake within healthy limitations, there is no reason you shouldnt enjoy a cup of frothy, buttery coffee goodness.
                      </p>
                     </div>
                     <!-- reply -->
                     <div class="reply">
                      <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/bulletproof-coffee/?replytocom=2485596#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-2485596", "2485596", "respond", "57146")'>

                  <div>
                   <div class="comment-body OneLinkNoTx">
                    <p>
                     it actually does, and carbs are not natural for us at all!  very few original vegetables had high carbs and fruit was only in season so we might have chomped on it here and there, but no way did we ever in our natural environment have fruit everyday, at least one piece, and 8 servings of high carb veggies, not to mention the whole wheat bread loaded with carbs that makes a well balanced diet.  If you lost weight doing high carbs you were likely busting your butt doing exercise to the point it almost killed you.  anyone can lose weight doing that.  but again, we werent meant to run hours a day, and we werent meant to lift weights endlessly.  We were meant to move naturally, with some hard work everyday, and walking but definitely we did not have world fitness gyms 300 years ago.
                    </p>
                    <p>
                     I always think its interesting looking at pictures from the 1920s, 30s, 40s, people are SLIM, not fat, the odd person was heavy, after the 40s, obesity started piling up, and now most people are fat.  Ketosis is just the body burning fat for fuel the way we have for millennia, instead of carbing ourselves to death!  Carbs also turn to sugar which spikes insulin which causes hypoglycemia which causes the falling asleep in the soup feeling and weakness and brain fog.  thats carbs, not fats.  Fats are the pure fuel your brain will use when carbs are nixed.  dont blame fats at all.  that is misinformation.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <!-- reply -->

                     The recipe is meant to replace your sugar and milk, so Id recommend giving it a try sans sugar first!
                     <br/>
                     ~Katelin
                    </p>

                  Sep 12, 2014
                 </a>
                 <!-- reply -->
                </div>
                <!-- .reply -->
                <div>
                 <div class="comment-body OneLinkNoTx">
                  <p>
                   Dave Asprey got found out to be a fraud about a year ago. He claims his coffee is the only one which is mycotoxins free. An independent lab went out and sampled numerous popular brands and found no less mycotoxins in Daves coffee as others on the market. The guy created a problem and then offered his coffee as a solution. He is a snake oils salesman.
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   Dont be expecting any magical benefits to putting oil in your coffee such as claims as kick starts the fat burning process!, Slow release energy!.. basically you are adding significant calories to your beverage. If weight loss is your main goal, be wise when choosing to drink your calories instead of eating them.
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   On a positive note, coconut oil+coffee+cinnamon is delicious
                   <img alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://blog.lululemon.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif"/>
                  </p>

                 <!-- reply -->
                </div>
                <!-- .reply -->
                <div>
                 <div class="comment-body OneLinkNoTx">
                  <p>
                   The version we make, which we call fatty-latte, consists of coffee, grass fed butter, coconut oil and double cream (to which I like to add a teaspoon of raw honey). Without the honey its around 400 calories of which 97% are from the 45g fat, 32 of them saturated. We also use a battery-powered mini-frother to avoid the fuss of heating and washing a blender. Its delicious, very satisfying and really helps with our ketogenic lifestyle.
                  </p>

                   <div class="comment-body OneLinkNoTx">
                    <p>
                     Hi Anna,
                     <br/>
                     Heres a note from Aleksandra on this: Adding cream, milk, nut milk, sugar, or honey WRECKS the affects  The glorious effects of drinking Bulletproof Coffee, like better brain function, increased energy, and normalized weight, can be cancelled out when things like cream, milk, nut milk, sugar, and honey are added to the recipe. Each of these foods change insulin response, stop autophagy, or cause inflammation. These physiological/biochemical changes in your body equals a foggy brain, hunger, and fat gain. No thank you!
                    </p>
                    <p>
                     ~Katelin
                    </p>

             <li class="comment odd alt depth-2" id="li-comment-2368064">
              <div class="offset1 span8">
               <div class="comment-container" id="comment-2368064">
                <div class="row">
                 <div class="comment-author vcard span3">
                  <div class="row">
                   <div class="span1">
                    <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-64 photo" height="64" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/6ece4da9ea9247cefbc3bea9cc28e041?s=64&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2F0.gravatar.com%2Favatar%2Fad516503a11cd5ca435acc9bb6523536%3Fs%3D64&amp;r=PG" width="64"/>
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                 <!-- .comment-author .vcard -->
                 <div class="comment-content span5">
                  <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata comment-author-name comment-date span2">
                   <!-- author name -->
                   <cite class="fn OneLinkNoTx">
                    Karen
                   </cite>
                   <!-- date -->
                   <a href="http://blog.lululemon.com/bulletproof-coffee/#comment-2368064">
                    Jan 4, 2015
                   </a>
                   <!-- reply -->
                  </div>
                  <!-- .reply -->
                  <div>
                   <div class="comment-body OneLinkNoTx">
                    <p>
                     Butter is the fat from the cream.  In processing (or churning) the cream, the fat and the milk separate  The fat is butter; the milk is buttermilk.  Both can be bought at wherever you buy groceries.  There is very little actual milk left in butter but if you are extremely lactose intolerant, then make ghee.  There are instruction online.  It separates the little bit of milk from the fat (butter).
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <!-- reply -->
                   <div class="reply">

                   I suggest slathering the Kerrygold butter over an already butter-laden croissant, add a spoonful of homemade or Bonne Maman Apricot Preserves, drink with fresh-brewed Cafe DuMonde chicory coffee and hot milk and tell everyone, your unconnected doctor included, to go to hell.
                  </p>

                <div>
                 <div class="comment-body OneLinkNoTx">
                  <p>
                   I have been drinking bullet proof coffee for 5 months now.
                   <br/>
                   The method Ive been using is as follows:
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   1/2 tablespoon of organic, grass fed, pasturized butter
                   <br/>
                   1 tablespoon of organic, virgen, cold pressed, unrefined coconut oil
                   <br/>
                   1 cup of pure roast low acid organic french roast coffee
                   <br/>
                   1 tablespoon organic brown sugar
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   Blend all the ingredients in the magic bullet blender and consume
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   Pros: Immediate rush of energy, feeling of satiety, the brain kicks on, tastes awesome,
                   <br/>
                   helps with regularity, I can use it to replace my pre-workout supplements
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   Cons: None so far
                  </p>
                 </div>
